      20  **Terminology: "Intent Capsule" is the public-facing term.** OW
          ASP's ASI01 mitigation #5 names "intent capsule" as the emergin
          g pattern for binding declared goal, constraints, and context t
          o each execution cycle in a signed envelope, which is what AIR 
          writes. Lead external comms (README, blog, pitch) with "Signed 
          Intent Capsule." The record-level Python types (`AgDRRecord`, `
          AgDRPayload`, `packages/projectair/src/airsdk/agdr.py`) stay na
          med AgDR for format compatibility with the accountability.ai/me
          2resh spec, but describe them as "AgDR-format-compatible Intent
           Capsules" in docs. This defuses the naming-collision risk arou
          nd authorship claims on AgDR.

  Searched for 2 patterns, read 2 files, listed 1 directory (ctrl+o to expand)

⏺ I have enough orientation. Two detectors, two different tiers of difficulty:

  ASI03 Identity & Privilege Abuse (v0.3 target): Needs a declared-scope source
  to check agents' actions against. Simplest path: sidecar agent-registry
  (agent_id → {permitted_tools, privilege_tier, data_scope}) passed to air 
  trace, plus optional source_agent_id / privilege_tier fields in AgDRPayload
  (already extra="allow", no schema bump). Detector flags: signer-key/agent-id
  mismatch, tool call outside permitted_tools, and tier-exceeding escalation
  chains. Ships honest coverage for OWASP ASI03 examples #1–#4.

  ASI10 Rogue Agents (v0.4 target): Needs a behavioral baseline to compare
  against. Two paths: (a) declared-scope — agent registry extends with expected
  tool-set / time-window / fan-out envelope, detector flags deviations; (b)
  learned baseline — consume N prior traces, build per-agent statistical
  profile. (a) is v0.3/v0.4-tractable and honest; (b) is a v0.5+ research build.
   I'd ship (a) labelled as "behavioral-scope" detector and leave (b) on the
  roadmap.

  Main tradeoff: both rely on an external registry the user must define — no
  registry means both detectors are no-ops on existing traces. That's fine and
  honest, but it means we also need a registry schema + CLI plumbing (e.g. air 
  trace trace.log --agent-registry registry.yaml) before the detectors are
  useful. Alternative: infer a soft baseline from the trace itself
  (first-seen-agent's tool-set = its baseline), which is zero-config but weak.

  Proposed sequence for this session:
  1. Land ASI03 end-to-end (detector + registry loader + CLI flag + tests + docs
   + version bump to 0.3.0).
  2. Land ASI10 as the declared-scope variant (extend the same registry, new
  detector, tests, docs).
  3. Publish 0.3.0 after (1), 0.4.0 after (2). Or one combined 0.3.0 if you want
   the "10 of 10" headline in a single release.

  Pick:
  - A. Ship both in a single 0.3.0 release (faster to "10 of 10" claim, fewer
  release artifacts).
  - B. Two releases (0.3.0 ASI03, then 0.4.0 ASI10) — cleaner version semantics,
   lets each detector settle before the next.
  - C. Something else — external registry approach, schema change to AgDR v0.3,
  or a different detector scope.

  Which way?

⏺ Plan: Vindicara 0.3.0 as the evidentiary layer for agentic AI

  Minor: "2016" is almost certainly 2026. Proceeding on that; correct me if I'm
  wrong.

  Strategic frame. Detector count is a checklist fight. Lakera, Guardrails,
  CalypsoAI can all ship ASI03/ASI10 detectors in a quarter if they want to. The
   moat is the signed chain itself, because it's math, not prompts, and it's the
   only substrate that produces court-ready, tamper-evident, chain-of-custody
  evidence. 10/10 OWASP is the headline. The category-defining move is pairing
  it with artifacts only AIR can emit because the chain exists. Positioning
  shift: "forensic reconstruction for AI agents" → "the evidentiary layer for 
  agentic AI compliance."

  That reframes Vindicara from "another detector library" (crowded) to "the
  signed source-of-truth for agent behavior" (one vendor per category).

  Phase 1. ASI03 Identity & Privilege Abuse

  Declared-scope detector. Sidecar agent registry (YAML/JSON) loaded via
  --agent-registry. Optional source_agent_id / privilege_tier in AgDRPayload
  (already extra="allow", no schema bump, AgDR format-compat preserved). Three
  findings:
  - identity forgery — signer_key does not match the registered public key for
  source_agent_id
  - out-of-scope tool — tool_name not in agent's permitted_tools
  - privilege escalation — tool requires tier > declared tier, or cross-agent
  handoff expands scope

  Maps to OWASP ASI03 examples #1–#4 honestly. No learned-anything; pure
  declared-policy enforcement.

  Phase 2. ASI10 Rogue Agents, framed as Zero-Trust-for-Agents

  Framing is load-bearing and I will not drift from it. This is enforcement of a
   declared behavioral envelope, not anomaly detection. The registry extends
  with expected tool-set, fan-out limit, data-domain scope, session time-window.
   Detector flags deviation from the envelope. Code comments, docstrings,
  README, HN post all say Zero-Trust enforcement — never anomaly detection. HN
  smells overclaim on learned baselines in under a minute; we don't give them
  the opening.

  Maps to ASI10 examples where a rogue agent operates outside its charter. The
  real learned-baseline variant (statistical profile, peer comparison) is
  explicitly a v0.5+ roadmap item. We say so in the docs.

  Phase 3. EU AI Act Article 72 evidence generator

  This is the 2026-product move. August 2, 2026 is the regulatory forcing
  function inside the runway. air report --article-72 trace.log emits a
  post-market-monitoring template populated from capsule data: incident
  timeline, system identifier, severity, corrective actions, signature integrity
   attestation. Procurement unlock for regulated industries. Cannot be
  reproduced without a signed chain, which means it cannot be copied by anyone
  but us in Q2 2026.

  This is the artifact that converts "10/10 detectors" (a feature) into "the
  signed evidentiary layer for Article 72" (a category).

  Phase 4. Pre-launch polish

  1. pip install projectair && air demo on three clean machines (macOS, Linux,
  fresh venv). Fix any friction. Highest-ROI 30 minutes in the sprint.
  2. Copy pass: README, site, HN post lead with "evidentiary layer for agentic
  AI" + 10/10 OWASP Agentic + Article 72. Flight-recorder / black-box analogy on
   the site.
  3. AIR Cloud waitlist signup on the site (captures intent, ships no product).

  Release

  Single 0.3.0 with all three shipped together. Headline: "10 of 10 OWASP
  Agentic + EU AI Act Article 72 evidence." Companion blog post: "Zero-Trust for
   Agents: ASI03, ASI10, and the evidentiary layer the EU AI Act actually asks 
  for."

  Explicit anti-scope this sprint

  No AIR Cloud, no MCP scanner expansion, no LlamaIndex/CrewAI/AutoGen, no
  learned-baseline ASI10, no AgDR schema bump.

  ---
  Before I start writing code, I need three answers:

  1. HN launch date and HF0 pitch date? Scope depends on time-box. Everything
  above fits ~10-14 days of focused work. If you have <7 days, drop Phase 3 and
  ship 10/10 + polish only.
  2. Is the Article 72 generator a fit for 0.3.0, or do you want to hold it for 
  0.3.1 to keep the HN narrative focused on 10/10 coverage? (I lean
  ship-together, but it's a judgment call.)
  3. Registry format: YAML or JSON? Both work. YAML reads better for
  hand-authored policy; JSON avoids another dependency if PyYAML isn't already
  in the wheel.

  Give me those three and I'll start on Phase 1 immediately.

           +tered claims.

      1153 +        if registered.signer_key.lower() != signer_key_lc:   
      1154 +            return None                                      
      1155 +        return registered                                    
      1156 +    return by_signer_key.get(signer_key_lc)                  
      1157 +                                                             
      1158 +                                                             
      1159 +def detect_identity_privilege_abuse(                         
      1160 +    records: list[AgDRRecord],                               
      1161 +    registry: AgentRegistry | None,                          
      1162 +) -> list[Finding]:                                          
      1163 +    """ASI03 Identity & Privilege Abuse: Zero-Trust-for-agent
           +s enforcement.                                               
      1164 +                                                             
      1165 +    OWASP Top 10 for Agentic Applications v12.6, ASI03. Check
           +s the signed                                                 
      1166 +    chain against an operator-declared ``AgentRegistry``. Thi
           +s detector is                                                
      1167 +    intentionally a **Zero-Trust enforcement** rule, not a le
           +arned-baseline                                               
      1168 +    anomaly detector: without a registry it returns no findin
           +gs, because AIR                                              
      1169 +    refuses to fabricate identity claims from an implicit mod
           +el.                                                          
      1170 +                                                             
      1171 +    Findings emitted:                                        
      1172 +                                                             
      1173 +      1. ``identity forgery`` (critical): a record claims ``s
           +ource_agent_id``                                             
      1174 +         X, the registry has X with signing key K, but the re
           +cord is signed                                               
      1175 +         with a different key. Covers OWASP ASI03 example #1 
           +(unauthorized                                                
      1176 +         agent impersonation) and example #2 (stolen or leake
           +d keys).                                                     
      1177 +      2. ``unknown agent`` (medium, dedup'd per agent_id): a 
           +record claims a                                              
      1178 +         ``source_agent_id`` that is not declared in the regi
           +stry. Covers                                                 
      1179 +         unregistered-agent activity in a policed environment
           +.                                                            
      1180 +      3. ``out-of-scope tool`` (high): a ``tool_start`` invok
           +es a tool that                                               
      1181 +         is not in the attributed agent's ``permitted_tools``
           +. Covers                                                     
      1182 +         example #4 (scope creep beyond declared authorisatio
           +n).                                                          
      1183 +      4. ``privilege escalation`` (critical): a ``tool_start`
           +` invokes a tool                                             
      1184 +         whose required tier (from ``tool_privilege_tiers``) 
           +exceeds the                                                  
      1185 +         attributed agent's ``privilege_tier``. Covers exampl
           +e #3 (privilege                                              
      1186 +         escalation via delegated task).                     
      1187 +                                                             
      1188 +    Attribution preference: a matching (claim, signing-key) p
           +air is trusted.                                              
      1189 +    A claim whose signing key does not match is flagged as fo
           +rgery and scope                                              
      1190 +    rules are suppressed for that record, so one bad identity
           + claim does not                                              
      1191 +    cascade into a pile of downstream "out-of-scope" noise.  
      1192 +    """                                                      
      1193 +    if registry is None or not registry.agents:              
      1194 +        return []                                            
      1195 +                                                             
      1196 +    findings: list[Finding] = []                             
      1197 +    by_id = {agent.id: agent for agent in registry.agents}   
      1198 +    by_signer_key = {agent.signer_key.lower(): agent for agen
           +t in registry.agents}                                        
      1199 +    flagged_unknown: set[str] = set()                        
      1200 +                                                             
      1201 +    for index, record in enumerate(records):                 
      1202 +        src = record.payload.source_agent_id                 
      1203 +                                                             
      1204 +        if src:                                              
      1205 +            registered = by_id.get(src)                      
      1206 +            if registered is None:                           
      1207 +                if src not in flagged_unknown:               
      1208 +                    flagged_unknown.add(src)                 
      1209 +                    findings.append(                         
      1210 +                        Finding(                             
      1211 +                            detector_id="ASI03",             
      1212 +                            title="Identity & Privilege Abuse
           +",                                                           
      1213 +                            severity="medium",               
      1214 +                            step_id=record.step_id,          
      1215 +                            step_index=index,                
      1216 +                            description=(                    
      1217 +                                f"Record claims source_agent_
           +id `{src}` but no agent with that "                          
      1218 +                                f"id is declared in the regis
           +try. Unregistered agent activity "                           
      1219 +                                f"in a policed environment (O
           +WASP ASI03)."                                                
      1220 +                            ),                               
      1221 +                        )                                    
      1222 +                    )                                        
      1223 +            elif registered.signer_key.lower() != record.sign
           +er_key.lower():                                              
      1224 +                findings.append(                             
      1225 +                    Finding(                                 
      1226 +                        detector_id="ASI03",                 
      1227 +                        title="Identity & Privilege Abuse",  
      1228 +                        severity="critical",                 
      1229 +                        step_id=record.step_id,              
      1230 +                        step_index=index,                    
      1231 +                        description=(                        
      1232 +                            f"Record claims source_agent_id `
           +{src}`, registered with signer_key "                         
      1233 +                            f"{registered.signer_key[:16]}...
           +, but the record is signed with "                            
      1234 +                            f"{record.signer_key[:16]}.... Po
           +ssible agent impersonation or "                              
      1235 +                            f"stolen key (OWASP ASI03 example
           + #1)."                                                       
      1236 +                        ),                                   
      1237 +                    )                                        
      1238 +                )                                            
      1239 +                                                             
      1240 +        attributed = _attribute_agent(record, by_id, by_signe
           +r_key)                                                       
      1241 +        if record.kind != StepKind.TOOL_START or attributed i
           +s None:                                                      
      1242 +            continue                                         
      1243 +                                                             
      1244 +        tool_name = record.payload.tool_name or ""           
      1245 +        if not tool_name:                                    
      1246 +            continue                                         
      1247 +                                                             
      1248 +        if not attributed.allows_tool(tool_name):            
      1249 +            findings.append(                                 
      1250 +                Finding(                                     
      1251 +                    detector_id="ASI03",                     
      1252 +                    title="Identity & Privilege Abuse",      
      1253 +                    severity="high",                         
      1254 +                    step_id=record.step_id,                  
      1255 +                    step_index=index,                        
      1256 +                    description=(                            
      1257 +                        f"Agent `{attributed.id}` invoked too
           +l `{tool_name}`, which is not in "                           
      1258 +                        f"its declared permitted_tools list. 
           +Scope creep beyond declared "                                
      1259 +                        f"authorisation (OWASP ASI03 example 
           +#4)."                                                        
      1260 +                    ),                                       
      1261 +                )                                            
      1262 +            )                                                
      1263 +                                                             
      1264 +        required_tier = registry.required_tier_for_tool(tool_
           +name)                                                        
      1265 +        if required_tier > attributed.privilege_tier:        
      1266 +            findings.append(                                 
      1267 +                Finding(                                     
      1268 +                    detector_id="ASI03",                     
      1269 +                    title="Identity & Privilege Abuse",      
      1270 +                    severity="critical",                     
      1271 +                    step_id=record.step_id,                  
      1272 +                    step_index=index,                        
      1273 +                    description=(                            
      1274 +                        f"Agent `{attributed.id}` (tier {attr
           +ibuted.privilege_tier}) invoked "                            
      1275 +                        f"tool `{tool_name}`, which requires 
           +tier {required_tier}. Privilege "                            
      1276 +                        f"escalation via delegated task (OWAS
           +P ASI03 example #3)."                                        
      1277 +                    ),                                       
      1278 +                )                                            
      1279 +            )                                                
      1280 +                                                             
      1281 +    return findings                                          
      1282 +                                                             
      1283 +                                                             
      1284 +def run_detectors(                                           
      1285 +    records: list[AgDRRecord],                               
      1286 +    registry: AgentRegistry | None = None,                   
      1287 +) -> list[Finding]:                                          
      1288 +    """Run every implemented detector and return a flat list 
           +of findings.                                                 
      1289 +

           +ero-Trust-for-                                               
      1291 +    agents detectors (ASI03 today; ASI10 on the roadmap) that
           + check the                                                   
      1292 +    signed chain against declared identity and scope. When om
           +itted, those                                                 
      1293 +    detectors return no findings rather than fabricating an i
           +mplicit                                                      
      1294 +    baseline.                                                
      1295 +    """                                                      
      1296      return [
      1297          *detect_goal_hijack(records),
      1298          *detect_tool_misuse(records),
      1299 +        *detect_identity_privilege_abuse(records, registry), 
      1300          *detect_prompt_injection(records),
      1301          *detect_sensitive_data_exposure(records),
      1302          *detect_mcp_supply_chain_risk(records),

❯ we have a new tagline .. i neeed you to stresstest it  "Forensic Incident Response for AI, Admissible by Design" 

⏺ Pausing code to stress-test the tagline properly.

  "Forensic Incident Response for AI, Admissible by Design"

  Verdict: 80% there. Two adjustments and it's the sharpest tagline in the 
  category. Unfixed, it has a landmine.

  What works (keep)

  - "Admissible by Design" is the single strongest phrase in any AI-security
  tagline I've seen. It maps directly to your actual architecture (Ed25519 +
  BLAKE3 + chain-of-custody), uses legal-grade vocabulary
  (GDPR/Privacy-by-Design resonance), and differentiates from every
  prevention-first competitor. Lakera, Guardrails, NeMo, Cisco AI Defense — none
   of them can claim this. It's a moat you own.
  - "Forensic Incident Response" is good buyer-clarity language. IR is a line
  item in every SOC budget. "Forensic" qualifies the type and ties to your
  signed-chain differentiator. Clean.
  - "by Design" not "by Default" — correct call. Architectural, not opt-in.
  Stronger.

  Where it's weak

  1. "for AI" is too broad. Fix: "for AI Agents" or "for Agentic AI."

  Your product does not secure AI models, it does not scan training pipelines,
  it does not inspect inference endpoints. It secures agents specifically —
  autonomous systems that take actions via tools. On a diligence call, an
  investor will ask "what's your scope?" and "AI" invites scope drift into
  territory you don't cover. Precision signals honest engineering. "For AI
  Agents" is tighter without losing punch.

  2. "Admissible by Design" is legally assertable, but right now it's 
  assertable-without-a-substrate. This is the landmine.

  I pressure-tested it against US Federal Rules of Evidence:
  - FRE 901 (Authentication): Ed25519 + BLAKE3 chain provides strong
  cryptographic authentication. ✓
  - FRE 902(14) (Self-authenticating electronic records): This is your hook.
  Records generated by an electronic process are self-authenticating if
  accompanied by a qualified certification. AIR's chain meets the technical bar.
   ✗ You haven't shipped the certification form or chain-of-custody procedure.
  - FRE 803(6) (Business records hearsay exception): machine-generated records
  qualify with proper foundation. ✓ Standard for any logging system.
  - Chain of custody: cryptographic signatures prevent in-chain tampering but
  don't prove the file wasn't replaced wholesale. That's procedural, not
  cryptographic.

  Translation: AIR ships the hardest technical primitive (authentication).
  What's missing is the documentation that turns "our chain is authenticable"
  into "our chain is presented in a court-admissible form."

  Before HN launch, ship a /admissibility page on vindicara.io that:
  - Maps AIR's primitives to FRE 901, 902(14), 803(6) by citation
  - Includes a sample certification template operators can file with a court
  - Documents chain-of-custody procedure (who holds the signing key, how is it
  rotated, how is the log preserved)
  - Acknowledges the jurisdictional scope (US FRE + EU eIDAS/Article 72)

  That page converts "Admissible by Design" from marketing into architecture.
  Without it, one HN lawyer asks "what does admissible mean?" and the thread
  turns.

  3. "Forensic Incident Response" is slightly off-register.

  Industry-standard phrasing is DFIR (Digital Forensics and Incident Response).
  "Forensic Incident Response" merges them into one phrase, which is defensible
  but non-standard. Some SOC buyers may parse it as "IR that happens to be
  forensic" rather than "the combined DFIR function." Low-severity, but be
  prepared to answer "do you do forensics, or IR, or both?" with "both —
  forensic evidence is what makes our IR actionable under regulation."

  International exposure

  "Admissible" is US-law vocabulary. In the EU, the equivalent is
  eIDAS-qualified electronic signatures (Article 25 of eIDAS grants legal effect
   equivalent to handwritten signatures only when issued by a qualified trust
  service provider). Raw Ed25519 without a QTSP is advanced-electronic-signature
   territory, not qualified. This is fine — EU AI Act Article 72 doesn't require
   qualified signatures, it requires auditable records. But the /admissibility
  page should say so explicitly, so you don't look ignorant in a German
  enterprise pitch.

  Recommended fix

  Hero (website + pitch): "Forensic Incident Response for AI Agents, Admissible
  by Design"

  Developer / PyPI: keep the current longer phrasing ("forensic reconstruction
  and incident response for AI agents") — "admissible by design" is an
  enterprise-motion claim, not a developer hook.

  Blocking work: /admissibility architecture page. ~1 page of copy, references
  to FRE sections, citation to Ed25519 RFC 8032 and BLAKE3 spec,
  chain-of-custody checklist. I can draft it inside Phase 4 if you want (takes
  ~45 min).

  Net

  Change "AI" → "AI Agents," ship the /admissibility doc before HN, and this
  tagline does more work than any other phrase on the site. Do not launch on HN
  without the doc — "admissible by design" without the substrate is the one line
   that could turn a supportive thread hostile.

  ---
  Continuing ASI03 plumbing. Registry module done, detector shipped into
  detections.py, pyproject.toml updated with PyYAML, dispatch wired through
  run_detectors(records, registry=None). Next: airsdk/__init__.py exports, then
  air trace --agent-registry CLI flag, then demo wiring.

      172 +def write_sample_registry(path: str | Path, signer_public_key_
          +hex: str) -> Path:                                            
      173 +    """Emit a sample agent registry that trips ASI03 against t
          +he demo chain.                                                
      174 +                                                              
      175 +    The registry declares one agent (``sales-agent-v1``) whose
          + signer_key is                                                
      176 +    the demo's main signing key and whose permitted_tools cove
          +r the benign                                                  
      177 +    sales-assistant tool surface. The chain's sensitive tools 
      178 +    (``admin_delete_records``, ``wire_transfer``, ``shell_exec
          +``) fall outside                                              
      179 +    the permitted set and are listed with a required tier abov
          +e the agent's                                                 
      180 +    tier, so they trip both out-of-scope and privilege-escalat
          +ion findings.                                                 
      181 +                                                              
      182 +    This is a Zero-Trust-for-agents demonstration, not a learn
          +ed baseline.                                                  
      183 +    The registry is operator-declared; the detector enforces i
          +t.                                                            
      184 +    """                                                       
      185 +    out_path = Path(path)                                     
      186 +    out_path.parent.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)        
      187 +    registry_data: dict[str, Any] = {                         
      188 +        "agents": [                                           
      189 +            {                                                 
      190 +                "id": DEMO_AGENT_ID,                          
      191 +                "signer_key": signer_public_key_hex,          
      192 +                "permitted_tools": [                          
      193 +                    "crm_read",                               
      194 +                    "rag_retrieve",                           
      195 +                    "read_file",                              
      196 +                    "email_draft",                            
      197 +                    "mcp_analytics.run_query",                
      198 +                    "python_eval",                            
      199 +                    "retry_api",                              
      200 +                    "draft_report",                           
      201 +                ],                                            
      202 +                "privilege_tier": 1,                          
      203 +            }                                                 
      204 +        ],                                                    
      205 +        "tool_privilege_tiers": {                             
      206 +            "admin_delete_records": 3,                        
      207 +            "wire_transfer": 3,                               
      208 +            "shell_exec": 3,                                  
      209 +        },                                                    
      210 +    }                                                         
      211 +    suffix = out_path.suffix.lower()                          
      212 +    if suffix in (".yaml", ".yml"):                           
      213 +        content = yaml.safe_dump(registry_data, sort_keys=Fals
          +e)                                                            
      214 +    elif suffix == ".json":                                   
      215 +        import json as _json                                  
      216 +        content = _json.dumps(registry_data, indent=2)        
      217 +    else:                                                     
      218 +        # Default to YAML if no recognised extension.         
      219 +        content = yaml.safe_dump(registry_data, sort_keys=Fals
          +e)                                                            
      220 +    out_path.write_text(content, encoding="utf-8")            
      221 +    return out_path

      1293 +def _parse_hour_utc(timestamp: str) -> int | None:           
      1294 +    """Extract the UTC hour (0..23) from an ISO 8601 timestam
           +p string.                                                    
      1295 +                                                             
      1296 +    Returns ``None`` on malformed input. AIR writes timestamp
           +s in UTC with a                                              
      1297 +    trailing ``Z``; this helper also accepts explicit ``+00:0
           +0`` offsets.                                                 
      1298 +    """                                                      
      1299 +    if not timestamp:                                        
      1300 +        return None                                          
      1301 +    value = timestamp.replace("Z", "+00:00")                 
      1302 +    try:                                                     
      1303 +        parsed = datetime.fromisoformat(value)               
      1304 +    except ValueError:                                       
      1305 +        return None                                          
      1306 +    return parsed.astimezone(UTC).hour                       
      1307 +                                                             
      1308 +                                                             
      1309 +def detect_rogue_agent(                                      
      1310 +    records: list[AgDRRecord],                               
      1311 +    registry: AgentRegistry | None,                          
      1312 +) -> list[Finding]:                                          
      1313 +    """ASI10 Rogue Agents: Zero-Trust behavioral-scope enforc
           +ement.                                                       
      1314 +                                                             
      1315 +    OWASP Top 10 for Agentic Applications v12.6, ASI10. Enfor
           +ces the                                                      
      1316 +    operator-declared ``BehavioralScope`` on each agent in th
           +e registry.                                                  
      1317 +    This detector is explicitly **Zero-Trust enforcement**, n
           +ot anomaly                                                   
      1318 +    detection against a learned baseline: findings only fire 
           +when an                                                      
      1319 +    agent's declared scope is breached. Without a declared sc
           +ope, no                                                      
      1320 +    findings are emitted.                                    
      1321 +                                                             
      1322 +    The learned-baseline variant (statistical profiling, peer
           + comparison                                                  
      1323 +    across agents) is not shipped in v0.3 and is scheduled fo
           +r a future                                                   
      1324 +    release. Shipping that variant responsibly requires a tra
           +ining-data                                                   
      1325 +    collection pattern AIR does not yet provide.             
      1326 +                                                             
      1327 +    Findings emitted, per agent whose registry entry declares
           + a                                                           
      1328 +    ``behavioral_scope`` block:                              
      1329 +                                                             
      1330 +      1. ``unexpected tool`` (high, dedup'd per (agent, tool)
           +): a                                                         
      1331 +         ``tool_start`` invokes a tool not in ``expected_tool
           +s``. The tool                                                
      1332 +         may be permitted by ASI03, but it is outside the age
           +nt's declared                                                
      1333 +         operational pattern. ASI10 flags *what the agent nor
           +mally does*;                                                 
      1334 +         ASI03 flags *what the agent is allowed to do*.      
      1335 +      2. ``fan-out breach`` (high, dedup'd per agent): the ag
           +ent has sent                                                 
      1336 +         ``agent_message`` records to more distinct targets t
           +han                                                          
      1337 +         ``max_fan_out_targets`` allows for the session.     
      1338 +      3. ``off-hours activity`` (medium): any record whose UT
           +C hour falls                                                 
      1339 +         outside ``allowed_hours_utc``.                      
      1340 +      4. ``session tool budget exceeded`` (high, dedup'd per 
           +agent): the                                                  
      1341 +         agent's cumulative ``tool_start`` count exceeds     
      1342 +         ``max_session_tool_calls``.                         
      1343 +                                                             
      1344 +    Attribution re-uses ``_attribute_agent`` so a forged-iden
           +tity record                                                  
      1345 +    (see ASI03) does not cascade into spurious ASI10 findings
           + against the                                                 
      1346 +    agent whose key was forged.                              
      1347 +    """                                                      
      1348 +    if registry is None or not registry.agents:              
      1349 +        return []                                            
      1350 +                                                             
      1351 +    findings: list[Finding] = []                             
      1352 +    by_id = {agent.id: agent for agent in registry.agents}   
      1353 +    by_signer_key = {agent.signer_key.lower(): agent for agen
           +t in registry.agents}                                        
      1354 +                                                             
      1355 +    tool_count: dict[str, int] = defaultdict(int)            
      1356 +    fan_out_targets: dict[str, set[str]] = defaultdict(set)  
      1357 +    flagged_unexpected: set[tuple[str, str]] = set()         
      1358 +    flagged_budget: set[str] = set()                         
      1359 +    flagged_fan_out: set[str] = set()                        
      1360 +                                                             
      1361 +    for index, record in enumerate(records):                 
      1362 +        attributed = _attribute_agent(record, by_id, by_signe
           +r_key)                                                       
      1363 +        if attributed is None or attributed.behavioral_scope 
           +is None:                                                     
      1364 +            continue                                         
      1365 +        scope = attributed.behavioral_scope                  
      1366 +        agent_id = attributed.id                             
      1367 +                                                             
      1368 +        if scope.allowed_hours_utc is not None and scope.allo
           +wed_hours_utc:                                               
      1369 +            hour = _parse_hour_utc(record.timestamp)         
      1370 +            if hour is not None and hour not in scope.allowed
           +_hours_utc:                                                  
      1371 +                findings.append(                             
      1372 +                    Finding(                                 
      1373 +                        detector_id="ASI10",

❯ Root cause: SvelteKit's static adapter emits pricing.html / blog.html / admissibility.html at the build root. The S3     
    website endpoint doesn't auto-append .html to extensionless paths, and there's no CloudFront function handling the     
    rewrite. So every direct URL hit (external link, SEO crawl, social share) hits 404. Internal nav on the home page uses 
     scroll-anchors, which is why nobody's tripped over this yet.                                                          
                                                                                                                           
    This blocks the entire traffic                                                                                         
  ⎿  Interrupted · What should Claude do instead?

❯ dont do anyhing                                                               

❯ tell me what to do instead                                                    
  ⎿  Interrupted · What should Claude do instead?

❯ 1. One-line SvelteKit config change: add trailingSlash: 'always' to prerender 
   config. Output becomes                                                       
    /pricing/index.html, /blog/index.html, /admissibility/index.html — S3's     
  default index-document behavior then serves                                   
    them at the extensionless URL. Fixes the whole site in one commit, no infra 
   changes.                                                                     
    2. CloudFront function: add a viewer-request function that rewrites /foo →  
  /foo.html. Pure infra change, build                                           
    untouch                                                                     

⏺ Recommendation: Option 1, with a 30-second verification.

  Why:
  - One commit, zero infra change, build pipeline untouched, no CloudFront
  function cold-start tax on every request
  - S3 static website hosting natively returns 302 /pricing → /pricing/ when it
  finds pricing/index.html but no pricing object, so old external links still
  resolve (after one redirect hop)
  - Google handles trailing-slash canonicalization cleanly; zero SEO penalty if
  you add <link rel="canonical"> (or rely on the 302)

  One thing to check first (matters for whether Option 1 works at all):

  Your CloudFront origin type. Two possibilities:
  - S3 website endpoint (vindicara-site.s3-website-us-east-1.amazonaws.com) →
  Option 1 works immediately. S3 website hosting serves index.html from
  directories and issues 302s for extensionless URLs. Done.
  - S3 REST endpoint / OAC origin (vindicara-site.s3.us-east-1.amazonaws.com) →
  Option 1 alone fails. REST endpoints don't do directory-index resolution.
  You'd need to switch the origin to the website endpoint OR add the CloudFront
  function anyway.

  Verify in CloudFront console: distribution → Origins tab → look at the "Origin
   domain" string. Website endpoints end in .s3-website-<region>.amazonaws.com;
  REST endpoints end in .s3.<region>.amazonaws.com.

  If website endpoint (most likely for an S3-hosted static site):

  1. In site/svelte.config.js, add:
  kit: {
    adapter: adapter({ /* existing */ }),
    prerender: { /* existing */ },
  }
  1. and in site/src/routes/+layout.ts add:
  export const trailingSlash = 'always';
  2. npm run build. Verify site/build/pricing/index.html,
  site/build/blog/index.html, site/build/admissibility/index.html exist.
  3. Deploy. curl -I https://vindicara.io/pricing should return 301/302 to
  /pricing/; curl -I https://vindicara.io/pricing/ should return 200.

  If REST endpoint, go Option 2 but write the function defensively:

  function handler(event) {
      var request = event.request;
      var uri = request.uri;
      if (uri === '/' || uri.includes('.')) return request;
      if (uri.endsWith('/')) uri = uri.slice(0, -1);
      request.uri = uri + '.html';
      return request;
  }

  Skipping uri.includes('.') handles /favicon.ico, /og-image.png, /robots.txt,
  /rss.xml, CSS, JS, fonts. Root stays untouched.

  Hybrid option if you want to avoid the 302 hop and keep clean URLs: do Option
  2 regardless of origin type. Adds ~0.5ms per request and ~$0.10 per million,
  but the URL shape stays /pricing with no redirect, which is marginally nicer
  for link previews and analytics. Your call on whether that matters enough to
  carry the infra.

  P0 severity is right. HN traffic arriving at a 404 is launch-killing. Fix
  before anything else today. Want me to also scan the blog posts / RSS feed /
  email signature / pitch deck for hardcoded non-trailing-slash links that'd
  benefit from a sweep?

      45  def _count_conversations(records: list[AgDRRecord]) -> int:
      46      finishes = sum(1 for r in records if r.kind == StepKind.AGE
          NT_FINISH)
      47      return max(finishes, 1)

      249 +    log: Path = typer.Argument(..., exists=True, readable=True
          +, help="Path to a JSON-lines AgDR log."),

      272 +        "--period",

      276 +        None,                                                 
      277 +        "--agent-registry",                                   
      278 +        help="Optional agent registry to enable ASI03/ASI10 Ze
          +ro-Trust enforcement during report generation.",              
      279 +        exists=True,

      281 +    ),                                                        
      282 +) -> None:                                                    
      283 +    """Generate an EU AI Act Article 72 post-market monitoring
          + report from an AgDR log.                                     
      284 +                                                              
      285 +    The output is a populated Markdown template, not a filed c
          +ompliance                                                     
      286 +    artefact. The provider must review, adapt, and have a qual
          +ified person                                                  
      287 +    sign the attestation before the report is legally usable. 
      288 +    """                                                       
      289 +    registry = _load_registry_or_exit(agent_registry)         
      290 +                                                              
      291 +    typer.secho(                                              
      292 +        f"[Article 72] Loading {log}...",                     
      293 +        fg=typer.colors.WHITE, bold=True,                     
      294 +    )                                                         
      295 +    records = load_chain(log)                                 
      296 +    conversations = _count_conversations(records)             
      297 +    verification = verify_chain(records)                      
      298 +    findings = run_detectors(records, registry=registry)      
      299 +                                                              
      300 +    report = ForensicReport(                                  
      301 +        air_version=airsdk_version,                           
      302 +        report_id=str(uuid4()),                               
      303 +        source_log=str(log.resolve()),                        
      304 +        generated_at=datetime.now(UTC).isoformat().replace("+0
          +0:00", "Z"),                                                  
      305 +        records=len(records),                                 
      306 +        conversations=conversations,                          
      307 +        verification=verification,                            
      308 +        findings=findings,                                    
      309 +    )                                                         
      310 +    markdown = generate_article72_report(                     
      311 +        report,                                               
      312 +        records,                                              
      313 +        system_id,                                            
      314 +        system_name=system_name,                              
      315 +        operator_entity=operator,                             
      316 +        monitoring_period=period,                             
      317 +    )                                                         
      318 +                                                              
      319 +    output.parent.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)          
      320 +    output.write_text(markdown, encoding="utf-8")             
      321 +                                                              
      322 +    if verification.status != VerificationStatus.OK:          
      323 +        typer.secho(                                          
      324 +            f"[WARNING] Chain verification did NOT pass: {veri
          +fication.reason}. "                                           
      325 +            "Review before relying on this report as evidence.
          +",                                                            
      326 +            fg=typer.colors.YELLOW, err=True,                 
      327 +        )                                                     
      328 +    else:                                                     
      329 +        typer.secho(                                          
      330 +            f"[Chain verified] {verification.records_verified}
          + signatures valid.",                                          
      331 +            fg=typer.colors.GREEN,                            
      332 +        )

✻ Churned for 6m 22s

❯ April 27: Public launch. SDK, CLI, vindicara.io live. OSS available           
  immediately.                                                                  
  60 days: First paying AIR Cloud customer at $1,499/mo.                        
  90 days: 500 GitHub stars, 100 weekly installs, 3 active design partner       
  conversations.                                                                
  6 months: 10+ paying teams, enterprise pipeline active, first LOI signed.     
  12 months: 50+ paying teams, SOC 2 Type I in progress, Series seed ready. is  
  this achevieable?                                                             

⏺ Honest answer: two of the five are high-probability if you execute well; three
   have real execution risk. Feasible as a whole, but you'll need to make scope
  calls along the way.

  Milestone-by-milestone

  April 27 — public launch (5 days from today)

  High risk, but achievable. Code is ready (0.3.0 all-green, 200 tests, 10/10
  Agentic live in the demo). What's tight:
  - Admissibility page needs to go live before HN launches. It's the moat behind
   the "Admissible by Design" tagline. If HN hits before the page is up, the
  tagline is assertable-without-a-substrate.
  - Linux install testing on a clean venv. Currently only smoke-tested on macOS.
   If pip install projectair fails on Ubuntu LTS, the launch thread dies in 20
  minutes.
  - HN post copy + LinkedIn + Twitter thread drafted and ready to fire.
  - Site copy rewritten to lead with "Project AIR: Forensic Incident Response
  for AI Agents, Admissible by Design" + "10 of 10 OWASP Agentic."
  - Logo integrated (still waiting on your path).

  Call: 5 days is doable if you don't add scope. If anything slips, push to May
  4 instead of shipping broken.

  60 days — first paying AIR Cloud customer at $1,499/mo

  Moderate risk. Two problems to solve in parallel:
  1. AIR Cloud doesn't exist yet. You need a minimum-viable hosted ingestion +
  dashboard + Square billing by week 6-7. That's real work.
  2. $1,499 is a price point you haven't validated. Your CLAUDE.md pricing
  ladder caps out at $499/Scale before Enterprise Custom. $1,499 is a new tier
  (Scale+? Lite-enterprise?). Is this a stated price or a target?

  Probability rises sharply if the first paying customer is a warm design 
  partner you've already been talking to pre-launch. From cold, 60 days is very
  aggressive for a $1,499 price point with a solo founder.

  Recommendation: start the design-partner pipeline right now, pre-launch. Three
   qualified conversations by launch day means you have a real shot at 60-day
  conversion. Zero conversations pre-launch and this slips to 90-120 days.

  90 days — 500 stars, 100 weekly installs, 3 design partner conversations

  Most achievable of the five if HN goes well. Benchmarks:
  - 500 stars in 90 days = Guardrails AI territory. Needs either one HN
  front-page hit OR sustained content (blog every 2-3 weeks)
  - 100 weekly installs = ~15/day. Modest. Natural if stars hit.
  - 3 design partner conversations = pure outreach effort, entirely controllable

  Biggest risk: if HN misses on launch day, you're in the sustained-content
  grind and 90-day stars is a stretch. One HN win de-risks all three sub-targets
   simultaneously.

  6 months — 10+ paying teams, enterprise pipeline active, first LOI

  Achievable with typical OSS-to-paid conversion velocity. 10 paying teams in 6
  months is a respectable-but-not-exceptional benchmark for a security tool with
   OSS top-of-funnel. First enterprise LOI requires 3+ month sales cycles, so
  expect LOI conversation starting month 2-3 to close by month 6.

  This milestone is the one that most depends on pricing-ladder velocity (free →
   $149 → $499 → Scale). If the Team tier differentiation (Agent IAM +
  behavioral baselines + 25 MCP servers) is genuinely valuable vs free,
  conversion works. If it's soft, 10 teams is a grind.

  12 months — 50+ paying teams, SOC 2 Type I in progress, Series seed ready

  Stretch goal. Getting from 10 to 50 teams in 6 months is 5x growth. That's
  upper-quartile SaaS trajectory. SOC 2 Type I takes 3-4 months of controls
  observation + audit; feasible to start at month 8-9.

  Series-seed-ready at month 11 means either (a) $20K-40K MRR + credible growth
  or (b) demand-side pull from inbound lead-investor interest. 50 teams at
  blended $200-$300 ARPU = $10K-$15K MRR, which is the low end of seed-stage
  traction. You'd want either higher-tier customers (enterprise LOIs converting
  to paid) or faster subscriber growth to make seed meetings easy.

  Where you'd need to cut scope if something slips

  In order of least-painful to most-painful:
  1. Drop April 27 → May 4. One-week slip doesn't break anything downstream.
  2. Reprice "first paying customer" from $1,499 to $499 or $999. Lower
  friction, still validates willingness to pay.
  3. Push SOC 2 Type I start to month 10-11. Still signals to seed investors.
  4. Reduce 12-month paying-team target from 50 to 30. Still credible traction.

  Don't cut: admissibility page at launch, honest detector framing,
  clean-machine install validation, pre-launch warm pipeline.

  My overall read

  You can hit four of five if execution stays tight. The one I'd downgrade to
  "stretch" is the 12-month seed readiness at 50 teams. $15K-ish MRR with a 5x
  trajectory curve is "good enough for some seed investors" but not "easy bar."
  Everything before month 6 is within reach if the launch goes well. Everything
  after depends on the cumulative effect of early months compounding.

  The single highest-leverage thing you can do between now and April 27: warm up
   3-5 design partner conversations. Every downstream milestone becomes ~30%
  more probable with that pipeline in place.

  What OSS ships (what you have today, from the code)

  - air CLI + airsdk (MIT)
  - All 10 OWASP Agentic detectors + 3 LLM + 1 AIR-native
  - LangChain / OpenAI / Anthropic instrumentation
  - Signed Intent Capsule chain (BLAKE3 + Ed25519, AgDR format)
  - Local JSON / PDF / SIEM (CEF) forensic exports
  - Agent registry (YAML/JSON) for ASI03/ASI10 Zero-Trust enforcement
  - Article 72 Markdown template generator (air report article72)
  - Chain verification + /admissibility architecture documentation

  That's a substantial free tier. It's the entire land.

  What Team $1,499/mo gates (AIR Cloud, what you'll build next)

  - Hosted dashboard, up to 25 agents
  - SIEM export (Datadog, Splunk, Sumo, Sentinel)
  - Incident workflows + alerting (Slack, email, PagerDuty, webhook)
  - Shared agent registry management (multi-user)
  - Cloud retention + cross-trace correlation
  - Email + Slack support

  What Enterprise $50K–$250K ACV gates

  - SSO / SAML / RBAC
  - Branded, regulator-ready PDF evidence (beyond OSS Markdown template)
  - Multi-system compliance aggregation (EU AI Act, SB 53, SOC 2, NIST AI RMF)
  - Insurance carrier integrations
  - On-prem / VPC / air-gapped deployment options
  - Dedicated IR contact, SLA, BAA
  - Unlimited agents and records

  competitors).

  branded/regulator-ready PDF + multi-system aggregation behind Enterprise?
  That's what your positioning needs — OSS distributes the moat, Enterprise

  How to record

  1. QuickTime Player (macOS, built-in): File → New Screen Recording → record a
  terminal window + browser tab.
  2. A fresh terminal with the current venv activated, large font (20pt+ so it
  reads at 480p).
  3. Pre-clear /tmp: cd /tmp && rm -f air-demo*.log air-demo-registry.yaml 
  forensic-report.json before starting.
  4. Record in one take; shorter edits are fine but single-take reads as
  authentic.
  5. Upload to YouTube as Unlisted, title "Project AIR — 60 second demo
  (unlisted)".

  Why this format over polished video

  - Authentic. HF0 / pitch reviewers see hundreds of AI demos; a real terminal
  capture of a working tool reads as substantive, not marketing.
  - No production time. Ship tonight.
  - The terminal IS the product for the OSS tier. Showing it working IS the
  pitch.

  Want me to:
  - A. Generate an exact shell script + text overlay notes you can follow during
   recording (30 min of your time to record + upload)?
  - B. Draft a tighter 45-second cut for attention-constrained viewers?
  - C. Something else?

⏺ Here's the exact script. Two decisions first, then the runbook.

  Pre-recording decisions

  1. Install scene: PyPI or skip?
  - projectair 0.3.0 is NOT yet on PyPI (you're eyeballing before upload).
  Current live version is 0.2.4, which shows 8/10 Agentic, not 10/10. Running
  pip install projectair on camera today installs the stale version.
  - Recommendation: Record AFTER you publish 0.3.0 so the pip install is real.
  That's roughly the next 15-30 minutes of your time (wheel build → twine check
  → upload → verify on PyPI simple index → record).
  - Alternative if you can't wait: Skip the install scene. Open in a terminal
  where air is already available. Caption: "$ air demo — takes 5 seconds after
  pip install projectair."

  2. One-take or edited?
  - One-take reads most authentic. Plan: ~75 seconds continuous, small stumbles
  are fine.
  - Edited (QuickTime + Trim) lets you cut dead air between sections. 60 seconds
   final. Looks slightly more produced.
  - My call: one-take unless you trip a command twice. Authentic > polished for
  this format.

  ---
  Pre-flight (5 min before recording)

  Terminal setup:
  - Open iTerm2 or Terminal.app, dark background
  - Font: Menlo 18pt or JetBrains Mono 18pt (brand-consistent with the site)
  - Window: 1280×720 minimum (YouTube 720p baseline)
  - Set prompt to just $ :
  export PS1='$ '
  clear

  Working directory prep:
  source /Users/KMiI/Desktop/vindicara/.venv-air/bin/activate
  cd /tmp
  rm -f air-demo.log air-demo-registry.yaml forensic-report.json
  article72-report.md
  clear

  Browser prep:
  - Tab 1: https://vindicara.io (homepage)
  - Tab 2: https://vindicara.io/admissibility/ (trailing slash — to avoid the
  302 flash on camera)
  - Both zoomed to 110% for readability
  - Browser window ready to switch to (Cmd+Tab rehearsal)

  QuickTime:
  - File → New Screen Recording
  - Options → Internal microphone off (silent video; text overlays in edit or
  YouTube captions)
  - Record the full screen at native resolution

  ---
  The 75-second script

  [0:00–0:05] Title card (add in YouTube editor or Keynote export)
  - Background: black
  - Text: "Project AIR"
  - Subtitle: "Forensic Incident Response for AI Agents, Admissible by Design"
  - Tiny caption bottom-right: MIT · pip install projectair · vindicara.io

  [0:05–0:10] Terminal enters frame. Clean prompt, nothing running.
  - Just sit for a beat so the viewer registers "this is real".

  [0:10–0:18] Install (skip if recording pre-PyPI).
  Type:
  pip install projectair
  Hit enter. Wait for the "Successfully installed projectair-0.3.0" line. Let
  that linger for 1 second.

  [0:18–0:22] Run the demo.
  Type:
  air demo
  Hit enter.

  [0:22–0:55] Let the output scroll. Do NOT scroll up. Do NOT narrate (you're
  silent). The visible output will include:
  - "Generating a fresh signed Intent Capsule chain..."
  - "Wrote sample to /tmp/air-demo.log"
  - "Chain verified: 47 signatures valid."
  - A stream of findings: ASI01 Agent Goal Hijack, ASI02 Tool Misuse, ASI03
  Identity & Privilege Abuse, ASI04 MCP Supply Chain, ASI05 RCE, ASI06 Memory
  Poisoning, ASI07 Inter-Agent, ASI08 Cascading Failures, ASI09 Human-Agent
  Trust, ASI10 Rogue Agents, AIR-01 Prompt Injection, AIR-02 Sensitive Data,
  AIR-03 Resource Consumption, AIR-04 Untraceable Action
  - The coverage table: "OWASP Top 10 for Agentic Applications coverage (10 
  implemented, 0 on roadmap)" — this is the hero frame. The scroll naturally
  lands here.
  - [Export] /private/tmp/forensic-report.json

  [0:55–1:00] Generate the Article 72 report.
  Type:
  air report article72 air-demo.log --system-id demo-sales-agent
  Let output print the "[Article 72] Wrote report" line.

  [1:00–1:08] Show the forensic report JSON briefly.
  Type:
  head -40 forensic-report.json
  Let the structured JSON scroll. Viewer sees "signature": "...",
  "content_hash": "...", "signer_key": "...", "verification": {"status": "ok"}.
  This is the evidence they walk away remembering.

  [1:08–1:18] Cmd+Tab to browser tab showing vindicara.io/admissibility/.
  - Scroll down once slowly so the FRE 901/902(13)/803(6) section headings are
  visible.
  - Stop at the "Sample Certification Template" heading. Let it sit for 2
  seconds.

  [1:18–1:25] Closing card (add in editor):
  - Black background
  - "10 of 10 OWASP Agentic + EU AI Act Article 72 + Admissible by Design"
  - "MIT · free forever · pip install projectair"
  - URL: vindicara.io

  [End at ~1:25]

  ---
  Post-recording checklist

  1. Trim the head and tail dead time in QuickTime (File → Edit → Trim).
  2. Add title + closing cards via iMovie, Keynote export-to-video, or just as
  YouTube text overlays in YT Studio.

    - Title: Project AIR — 60 second demo

    - Visibility: Unlisted
    - Thumbnail: a frame from the "10 implemented, 0 on roadmap" moment
  4. Test the link in an incognito window before pasting into the form.
  5. Paste the URL into the form.

  If you want to skip the Article 72 command (to cut to ~60 seconds)

  Cut [0:55–1:00] and [1:00–1:08]. Jump straight from the coverage table to the

  All three cut from the SAME recording. No re-shoots.

  Production quality checklist (the stuff that makes it "strongest")

  1. Font & contrast: Terminal at JetBrains Mono 24pt (brand-consistent with
  site), pure black background, bright white/green text. Forget fancy themes for
   this; plain reads clearest on mobile.
  2. Capture resolution: Record in full 2560×1440 or 1920×1080. You can always
  downsample; you cannot upsample.
  3. Cursor hygiene: Turn off rainbow cursor effects. Plain blinking block. Hide
   the mouse pointer during terminal sections using QuickTime's "Show Mouse
  Clicks" OFF.
  4. No Slack/email notifications: macOS Do Not Disturb ON. Unplug from Wi-Fi
  briefly if you're paranoid.
  5. Multiple takes: Record the 0:13–1:08 terminal section 3–5 times. Keep the
  cleanest one. You will absolutely fat-finger at least one take.
  6. Dead air between takes: Leave 2-second pauses between sections when
  recording — easier to cut later.
  7. Background music: For ad cuts, consider a subtle ambient track at -18 dB.
  Royalty-free: YouTube Audio Library has "Dark Cinematic" tracks that work.
  Master stays silent (HF0 reviewers prefer it).
  8. Captions burned in: For social ads (85% viewed muted), text overlays
  explaining what the terminal is doing. E.g., "Signed chain generated" when the
   chain output prints; "All 10 detectors firing" over the findings scroll; "EU
  AI Act Article 72 auto-generated" over the report command.
  9. Open-graph thumbnail: Grab a frame of the "10 implemented, 0 on roadmap"
  line. This is your social preview image.

  Voiceover: yes or no?

  Master version: yes, optional. A calm, flat narration over the demo adds 20%
  production quality for 30 minutes of your time. Script to read:

  ▎ (over the hook) "AI agents are writing code, sending money, and making 
  ▎ decisions. When something goes wrong, you need proof of what happened."
  ▎
  ▎ (over the install) "Project AIR is an MIT-licensed CLI and SDK that writes a
  ▎  signed, cryptographically verifiable record for every agent action."
  ▎
  ▎ (over the demo scroll) "Ten OWASP Agentic Applications detectors. EU AI Act 
  ▎ Article 72 evidence. One command."
  ▎
  ▎ (over the admissibility page) "Admissible by Design. The signed chain maps 
  ▎ to US Federal Rules of Evidence and EU eIDAS. Free, forever. Vindicara dot 
  ▎ io."

  Record on your laptop mic in a quiet room. Imperfect voiceover reads more
  authentic than polished; don't over-coach it.

  Social cuts: no voice. Muted autoplay. Text overlays do the work.

  Now — the thing blocking all of this is PyPI

  Ready to proceed? Two options:
  - A. I run the wheel build + twine check now and show you the output; you
  eyeball and run twine upload yourself. ~10 min.
  - B. Same as A but I also upload once you give the go. ~15 min total.

  Your call. After it's live on PyPI, wait 5 minutes for the simple index to
  propagate, then record.

❯ ~/.pypirc  how do i store it ? 

⏺ Walking you through the ~/.pypirc setup.

  Step 1 — Create the file:

  touch ~/.pypirc
  chmod 600 ~/.pypirc

  The chmod 600 matters: file contains a credential, must not be world- or
  group-readable.

  Step 2 — Open in a text editor:

  nano ~/.pypirc

  or any editor you prefer (vim, vscode, etc.). Do not paste the token into your
   shell — it'll land in history.

  Step 3 — Paste this exact content (with your real token):

  [pypi]
  username = __token__
  password = pypi-AgEIcHlwaS5vcmcC...your-real-token-here

  - The username is the literal string __token__ (with two underscores, not your
   email or a username)
  - The password is the entire PyPI token string including the pypi- prefix. Get
   it from https://pypi.org/manage/account/token/ if you need a fresh one.

  Step 4 — Save and close. (Ctrl+O then Enter, then Ctrl+X in nano.)

  Step 5 — Verify permissions:

  ls -l ~/.pypirc

  You should see -rw------- at the start. If it shows -rw-r--r-- or broader,
  re-run chmod 600 ~/.pypirc.

  Step 6 — Test with the upload:

  cd /Users/KMiI/Desktop/vindicara/packages/projectair
  python -m twine upload dist/projectair-0.3.0*

  Twine will pick up the credentials from ~/.pypirc automatically. No prompts.
  If the upload works, you're set for every future release.

  Security notes:
  - Never commit ~/.pypirc to git (it's in your home dir, not the repo, so
  you're fine by default).
  - Don't paste the token into Slack / email / anywhere searchable.
  - If you suspect the token leaked, revoke and regenerate it at
  https://pypi.org/manage/account/token/ immediately.

         +ite this exact taxonomy. Never revert to the "8 of 10" or "3 of
         + 10" framing from earlier releases.                            
      24 +- **ASI10 is Zero-Trust enforcement, not anomaly detection.** F
         +rame it as declared-scope enforcement in every doc, docstring, 
         +README, and HN post. The learned-baseline anomaly-detection var
         +iant (statistical profiling, peer comparison) is explicitly on 
         +the roadmap for a later release and is labelled as such in `det
         +ections.py`. Calling the shipped detector "anomaly detection" i
         +s overclaim and will attract HN skepticism in under a minute.  
      25  - **Do not conflate AIR-04 with ASI10.** AIR-04 detects gaps in
           our own chain (missing tool_end records, silent intervals). AS
          I10 Rogue Agents is about agents acting outside their authoriza
          tion scope / stealth infiltration. OWASP lists signed audit log
          s as a *mitigation* for ASI10, not a detection signal. Calling 
          AIR-04 "ASI10 coverage" is overclaim. If we want real ASI10 cov
          erage, we ship a behavioral-scope detector.
      26  
      27  **Terminology: "Intent Capsule" is the public-facing term.** OW
          ASP's ASI01 mitigation #5 names "intent capsule" as the emergin
          g pattern for binding declared goal, constraints, and context t
          o each execution cycle in a signed envelope, which is what AIR 
          writes. Lead external comms (README, blog, pitch) with "Signed 
          Intent Capsule." The record-level Python types (`AgDRRecord`, `
          AgDRPayload`, `packages/projectair/src/airsdk/agdr.py`) stay na
          med AgDR for format compatibility with the accountability.ai/me
          2resh spec, but describe them as "AgDR-format-compatible Intent
           Capsules" in docs. This defuses the naming-collision risk arou
          nd authorship claims on AgDR.

❯ i am thinking of reaching out to owasp association mentioning vindicara       

❯ what do you think                                                             

⏺ Yes, reach out — but make it substantive, not promotional. Timing matters:
  before HN launch, not after. OWASP recognition ahead of launch compounds
  credibility; after is just nice-to-have.

  Why this is worth doing now

  You just shipped the OSS reference implementation of OWASP Top 10 for Agentic
  Applications v12.6. All ten ASI categories mapped 1:1 to detectors in
  published code, MIT-licensed, verifiable against the spec. That is the exact
  contribution OWASP wants from the vendor/tool community — not a marketing
  pitch, but usable code that instantiates their taxonomy.

  The fact that memory shows "Scott Clinton outreach was unblocked at 5/10"
  means this was already on the roadmap. You've now doubled the coverage since
  then and shipped a complete Article 72 generator and the
  Zero-Trust-enforcement framing for ASI03/ASI10. Your outreach case is
  materially stronger today than it was four days ago.

  What works with OWASP, what doesn't

  What works:
  - Offering substance (code, mappings, research) rather than asking for
  something (endorsement, co-marketing).
  - Citing their spec by section (ASI01 mitigation #5 intent-capsule pattern) —
  demonstrates you've actually read it.
  - Explicitly stating MIT license + no OWASP trademark usage. They worry about
  OWASP-washing and you pre-emptively address it.
  - A clear, specific ask: Solutions Landscape submission, citation in reference
   implementations, speaking slot at AppSec, not "let's chat."

  What gets ignored or backfires:
  - Generic "we'd love to partner" language that reveals no homework.
  - Implying endorsement. OWASP does not endorse vendors; the taxonomy is
  vendor-neutral.
  - Marketing-forward language (10x, revolutionary, leader). Reads as spam.
  - Asking for a meeting before proving substance.

  The three angles, ranked

  1. Q3 Solutions Landscape submission (strongest, most concrete). This is a
  curated catalog of tools implementing Top 10 mitigations. At 10/10 coverage
  with an open-source reference implementation, you have a stronger case than
  almost anyone else in the landscape. Submission is a documented process, not a
   favor.
  2. Reference implementation citation in OWASP's own documentation. Offer
  Project AIR as the OSS example implementation of the signed intent-capsule
  pattern (ASI01 mitigation #5 explicitly names this as emerging). OWASP has
  historically accepted OSS reference implementations.
  3. Speaking proposal at OWASP AppSec or local chapter meetup. Technical talk:
  walk through how 10/10 ASI detection actually works on a signed chain. Live
  demo of air demo. This is a second-wave move, not a first-email ask.

  Best approach: send ONE email that opens with #1 and #2, references #3 as a
  later conversation.

  The risk angle

  One landmine I'd pressure-test: OWASP trademark use. The taxonomy names
  (ASI01, ASI10, etc.) are OWASP's. You reference them heavily in code, docs,
  the admissibility page, and marketing. Standard practice is fine (you cite by
  number and full name, clearly attribute the taxonomy), but if anything on the
  site implies OWASP endorsement, they'll push back. Quick audit before sending:
  - Does anything on vindicara.io say "OWASP-certified" or "OWASP-approved"?
  (Both are forbidden.)
  - Does the README claim OWASP partnership? (It shouldn't.)
  - The /admissibility page references FRE + eIDAS — OWASP isn't implied there.
  Clean.
  - The pricing page, homepage — verify no "OWASP" branding beyond citation of
  the taxonomy by name.

  If any of those slip in, fix them before emailing OWASP. They'll Google you
  before responding.

  Email draft (want me to write it?)

  I'll draft something in the ~200 word range, substantive, with the right tone.
   Structure:

  1. Opening one-line: "We've built the open-source reference implementation of
  OWASP Top 10 for Agentic Applications v12.6, covering all 10 ASI categories
  under MIT license."
  2. Evidence (links):
    - PyPI: pip install projectair → live at
  https://pypi.org/project/projectair/0.3.0/
    - GitHub: https://github.com/get-sltr/vindicara-ai
    - Detector-to-ASI mapping (I'd produce this as a one-page table before
  sending)
    - /admissibility page as the architecture doc
  3. Specific asks (two):
    - Solutions Landscape Q3 submission: what's the right process?
    - Is there interest in referencing Project AIR in the Top 10 docs as an
  example implementation of the signed intent-capsule pattern (ASI01 mitigation
  #5)?
  4. Low-friction close: "Happy to provide any additional detail, walkthrough,
  or direct code reference. MIT license means zero legal entanglement for
  OWASP."

  Want me to draft the actual text plus prepare the one-page detector-to-ASI
  mapping table as an attachment? Takes me about 20 minutes. Then you review and
   send it yourself.

  Separately: do you know who to send it to? Memory mentions Scott Clinton
  (project lead for OWASP Top 10 for LLM / Agentic Applications). If you have
  his email, we use it. If not, the OWASP project page usually lists a contact
  or a GitHub org where maintainers respond to issues/discussions.

  ---
  Subject: Open-source reference implementation for OWASP Top 10 for Agentic
  Applications (10/10 ASI coverage, MIT)

  To: Rachel James (OWASP ASI lead)
  Cc: Steve Wilson, Ken Huang

  Rachel, Steve, Ken,

  I'm Kevin Moore, founder of Vindicara. I'm writing because we've shipped what
  we believe is the first open-source reference implementation of the OWASP Top
  10 for Agentic Applications v12.6, with detectors for all ten ASI categories
  plus three OWASP LLM Top 10 categories, MIT-licensed and available on PyPI
  today.

  The project is Project AIR (pip install projectair). It writes a BLAKE3 +
  Ed25519 signed Intent Capsule chain for every agent action (the emerging
  pattern you name in ASI01 mitigation #5) and runs detectors for ASI01 through
  ASI10 on replay. ASI03 Identity & Privilege Abuse and ASI10 Rogue Agents are
  implemented as Zero-Trust enforcement against an operator-declared agent
  registry, not as learned-baseline anomaly detection; we're explicit about that
   scope in the docs to avoid overclaim.

  Two specific asks:

  1. Solutions Landscape submission. We'd like to submit Project AIR for the
  OWASP Top 10 for Agentic Applications Solutions Landscape. What's the right
  process and timing for that?
  2. Reference implementation citation. The Top 10 docs currently describe the
  signed intent-capsule pattern as "emerging." If helpful, we'd be glad to be
  referenced as an open-source example implementation. MIT license means there
  is no legal entanglement for OWASP.

  Links:
  - PyPI: https://pypi.org/project/projectair/0.3.0/
  - GitHub: https://github.com/get-sltr/vindicara-ai
  - Admissibility architecture doc (BLAKE3 + Ed25519 mapped to US FRE
  901/902(13)/803(6) and EU eIDAS / AI Act Article 72):
  https://vindicara.io/admissibility/
  - Detector-to-ASI source mapping (code-level, annotated): https://github.com/g
  et-sltr/vindicara-ai/blob/main/packages/projectair/src/airsdk/detections.py

  Happy to walk through the implementation or provide any additional detail.
  Appreciate the work the three of you have done on the taxonomy — we've built
  against it carefully, and it shows.

  Best,

  LinkedIn draft (~1500 characters)

  Project AIR 0.3.0 is live on PyPI today.

  An open-source reference implementation of the OWASP Top 10 for Agentic
  Applications v12.6. All ten ASI categories shipped, MIT-licensed.

  ASI01 Agent Goal Hijack
  ASI02 Tool Misuse & Exploitation
  ASI03 Identity & Privilege Abuse
  ASI04 Agentic Supply Chain Vulnerabilities
  ASI05 Unexpected Code Execution
  ASI06 Memory & Context Poisoning
  ASI07 Insecure Inter-Agent Communication
  ASI08 Cascading Failures
  ASI09 Human-Agent Trust Exploitation
  ASI10 Rogue Agents

  Plus three OWASP LLM Top 10 detectors (prompt injection, sensitive data
  exposure, model DoS) and one AIR-native chain-integrity check.

  Every agent action produces a BLAKE3-hashed, Ed25519-signed Intent Capsule,
  chained to the previous record. Alter any byte and verification breaks
  deterministically at the exact step.

  Also shipped:
  • EU AI Act Article 72 evidence generator (one command)
  • Admissibility by Design architecture, with FRE and eIDAS mappings
  • LangChain, OpenAI, Anthropic framework instrumentation
  • Offline signature verification, no cloud dependency

  When an AI agent sends the wrong wire, leaks the wrong file, or approves the
  wrong thing, the question that matters is not "did we try to stop it?" It's
  "can you prove what happened, in a form your legal team, auditor, regulator,
  and insurance carrier will accept?"

  That's what Project AIR is for.

  pip install projectair
  https://vindicara.io/admissibility/
  https://github.com/get-sltr/vindicara-ai

  #AISecurity #OWASP #AgenticAI #AIGovernance #EUAIAct
